Removing Access
These are the steps on how to remove access from NimUI.

Go to Opnext and login, then return here [OPNEXT].
Check if the user is defined and/or active:

SELECT ID, USERNAME, EMAIL, STATUS FROM COMMON.USERS WHERE EMAIL = '<EMAIL_ADDRESS>';
Remove if the user is listed:

UPDATE COMMON.USERS SET STATUS = 'D' WHERE EMAIL = '<EMAIL_ADDRESS>' AND ID = <ID_VALUE_FROM_PREV_STEP> ;




next is NimUI, above is the SOC SOP for removing and adding access as well as the current script updated from python2 that was used 5 years ago to check and remove access
import logging
import requests
import json
import secret

# Setup logging
logging.basicConfig(
    format="%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s",
    level=logging.INFO
)

# PagerDuty API Configuration
API_KEY = secret.get_secret("_PAGERDUTY_API_KEY")
URL = "https://api.pagerduty.com/users"

HEADERS = {
    "Authorization": f"Token token={API_KEY}",
    "Accept": "application/vnd.pagerduty+json;version=2",
    "Content-Type": "application/json"
}

def check_pagerduty_access(username, mock_mode):
    """Check if a user has access to PagerDuty (mocked when MOCK_MODE=True)."""
    if mock_mode:
        logging.info(f"[MOCK] Simulating PagerDuty access check for {username}.")
        return [{"id": "MOCK_USER_ID", "name": username}] if username in ["mockuser", "testuser"] else None

    params = {"query": username}
    
    try:
        response = requests.get(URL, headers=HEADERS, params=params)
        response.raise_for_status()
        data = response.json()

        users = data.get("users", [])
        return users if users else None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"Failed to fetch PagerDuty user data: {e}")
        return None

def remove_pagerduty_access(user_id, mock_mode):
    """Remove user from PagerDuty (mocked when MOCK_MODE=True)."""
    if mock_mode:
        logging.info(f"[MOCK] Would remove user with ID {user_id} from PagerDuty.")
        return  # Skip actual deletion in mock mode

    delete_url = f"{URL}/{user_id}"
    
    try:
        response = requests.delete(delete_url, headers=HEADERS)
        response.raise_for_status()

        if response.status_code == 204:
            logging.info(f"✅ Successfully removed user with ID {user_id} from PagerDuty.")
        else:
            logging.warning(f"⚠️ Unexpected response while removing user {user_id}: {response.status_code}")
    
    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"Failed to remove PagerDuty user: {e}")

def foundAccess(user, accessChoice, mock_mode):
    """Handle found access logic (mocked when MOCK_MODE=True)."""
    user_data = check_pagerduty_access(user, mock_mode)
    
    if user_data:
        user_id = user_data[0]["id"]
        
        if accessChoice == "check":
            logging.info(f"✅ {user} has PagerDuty access.")
        elif accessChoice == "remove":
            logging.info(f"⚠️ {user} has PagerDuty access. Removing...")
            remove_pagerduty_access(user_id, mock_mode)
    else:
        logging.info(f"❌ {user} does NOT have PagerDuty access.")

def main(user, creds):
    """Check or remove PagerDuty access for a given user."""
    mock_mode = creds["MOCK_MODE"]  # Read Mock Mode from creds

    foundAccess(user, creds["accessChoice"], mock_mode)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    logging.info("Checking PagerDuty access...")

    username = input("Enter LDAP username to check/remove: ").strip()
    accessChoice = input("Would you like to check or remove access? (Check/Remove): ").strip().lower()

    while accessChoice not in ("check", "remove"):
        accessChoice = input("Invalid input. Please enter 'Check' or 'Remove': ").strip().lower()

    creds = {
        "accessChoice": accessChoice,
        "MOCK_MODE": True  # This would be overridden when called from separations.py
    }

    main(username, creds)

Description
This SOP is for adding and removing access for the Pager Duty.

 Service Account & Password found in Keypass

Fill out First Name, Email address and Base Role 
* Base role for most people is "stakeholder"
* Base role for engineer is "Observer"
You are welcome to add a Team now if it is included in the request.
Then click the green Add button.

5. Then click the "Send Invitations" button.

next is pagerduty
and the last of the old scripts being updated is rt_tickets.py




import logging
import secret
import rt
from rt_marchex import rtbroker

# Setup logging
logging.basicConfig(
    format="%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s",
    level=logging.INFO
)

# Retrieve RT Credentials
RT_USER = secret.get_secret('_SOC_UI_USER')
RT_PASS = secret.get_secret('_SOC_UI_PASS')

# RT Server Info
RT_HOST = "https://rt.marchex.com"
RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"

RT_QUERY = (
    "Owner = '{user}' "
    "AND ( Status = 'new' OR Status = 'open')"
)

def loginToRT(mock_mode):
    """Log into the RT Ticketing system (mocked when MOCK_MODE=True)."""
    if mock_mode:
        logging.info("[MOCK] Skipping real RT login.")
        return None  # Avoid actual login

    tracker = rt.Rt(RT_URL, RT_USER, RT_PASS)
    if not tracker.login():
        logging.error("❌ Failed to log in to RT.")
        return None
    return tracker

def main(user, creds):
    """Search for open tickets assigned to a given user in RT (mocked when MOCK_MODE=True)."""
    mock_mode = creds["MOCK_MODE"]  # Read Mock Mode from creds

    if mock_mode:
        logging.info(f"[MOCK] Simulating RT query for {user}.")
        # Simulated tickets for testing
        tickets = {
            "RT-1234": "Mock Ticket 1 - Access Request",
            "RT-5678": "Mock Ticket 2 - Permissions Issue"
        } if user in ["mockuser", "testuser"] else None
        return (tickets, user, creds)

    try:
        rtb = rtbroker(RT_HOST)
        rtb.loginUser(RT_USER, RT_PASS)

        tickets = rtb.ticket_search(RT_USER, RT_QUERY.format(user=user))
        
        return (tickets, user, creds) if tickets else (None, user, creds)

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error querying RT for {user}: {e}")
        return (None, user, creds)

def foundAccess(result):
    """Determine if a user has RT tickets and handle removal if needed."""
    if result[0] is not None:
        accessChoice = result[2]["accessChoice"]
        mock_mode = result[2]["MOCK_MODE"]

        if accessChoice == "check":
            logging.info(f"📌 RT Tickets found for {result[1]}:")
            for key, val in result[0].items():
                logging.info(f"🔹 {key}: {val}")

        elif accessChoice == "remove":
            logging.warning(f"⚠️ Attempting to reassign tickets for {result[1]}")
            stealTickets(result, mock_mode)

def stealTickets(result, mock_mode):
    """Reassign RT tickets from the user to another queue (mocked when MOCK_MODE=True)."""
    if mock_mode:
        logging.info(f"[MOCK] Would reassign {len(result[0])} tickets from {result[1]}.")
        for ticket_id in result[0].keys():
            logging.info(f"[MOCK] Successfully reassigned ticket {ticket_id}.")
        return

    tracker = loginToRT(mock_mode)
    if not tracker:
        logging.error("❌ Unable to proceed with ticket reassignment due to login failure.")
        return

    for ticket_id in result[0].keys():
        try:
            tracker.edit_ticket(ticket_id, Queue="SOC")
            tracker.steal(ticket_id)
            tracker.edit_ticket(ticket_id, Owner=RT_USER, Queue="Production")
            logging.info(f"✅ Successfully reassigned ticket {ticket_id} from {result[1]}.")
        except Exception as e:
            logging.error(f"❌ Failed to reassign ticket {ticket_id} from {result[1]}: {e}")

def main_prompt():
    """Prompt user for input and initiate RT ticket separation process."""
    logging.info("🔍 Checking RT Tickets")
    
    sepList = input("Enter LDAP user(s) to be separated (comma-separated): ").split(",")
    accessChoice = input("Would you like to check or remove access? (Check/Remove): ").strip().lower()

    while accessChoice not in ("check", "remove"):
        accessChoice = input("Invalid input. Please enter 'Check' or 'Remove': ").strip().lower()

    creds = {
        "accessChoice": accessChoice,
        "MOCK_MODE": True  # This would be overridden when called from separations.py
    }

    for user in sepList:
        result = main(user.strip(), creds)
        foundAccess(result)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main_prompt()





SOC SOP uiRT

Description
This SOP is for adding and removing access for the RT.

Corp IT continues to own the RT product, however, the SOC has been empowered to add or remove users as needed. There are many times when we need to give an RT to someone, but they aren't in the production queue so we have to give the tickets to someone on their team and send a ticket to Corp IT to add them to RT. No more! Now we can add them ourselves.



Adding AccessRemoving AccessOther RT Info


1. First open a ticket and document getting permission to add the user from their manager
2. Once you have a ticket with permission to add the user:
Open RT
Go to Tools -> configuration -> users -> select
Click the user / search for the user and click them
Next there is membership tab right top corner
There are only 2 queues we will be using.

If the person is on media engineering, use the media-engineering-team
If the person isn't on media engineering, use "production-workers-non-ops"
At the top right hit members
To add: If we ever need to assign a ticket to someone that isn't in RT, feel free to add them to the queue

Go to Tools -> configuration -> users-> select
Next there is membership tab right top corner

If the person isn't on media engineering, use "production-workers-non-ops"
At the top right hit members
To Remove: Look through the list and check mark the person that doesnt work here anymore and then hit "Modify Members" in the bottom right and it will remove them from the group




Other RT Info


Corp IT still owns this product, but this SOP lets us add people if we need to give someone a ticket.

ADMINS:

admins get an email when the ticket is opened
admins also get an email for every single update that is done to the ticket


WORKERS:

workers get an email that a ticket was opened

We'll add people to production-workers-non-ops; which makes them a worker (see definition above). They can be assigned tickets in the production queue, but they don't get notifications about tickets in the production queue. This is the main one that everybody is in.

Some general knowledge that doesn't really fit into a specific tab but it's good to have


Auth0 is used for clients to connect to Marchex's UIs, APIs, and platforms using their own credentials.
In some cases such as marchex-one-ui, some other services will get to apply their tokens on their behalf.


SOC account credentials in BitWarden


There are three different kinds of access that may be asked for:
Enterprise Connections
Applications
Individual Users


There are logs available if people have a hard time logging on and want us to dig in:
Go here!
You can search by connection name like:
 connection: <Name Here> 
so if someone needs you to look for specific logs regarding a client to see why something might be failing, that's the easiest way to do it.



If you need to send any service-related email to Auth0, use the prod tenant

SOC SOP uiAuth0
SOC SOP uiNimUI | SOC SOP uiAccessPagerDuty | SOC SOP uiRT | SOC SOP uiAccessAFR | SOC SOP uiAuth0
Jump to navigationJump to search


GeneralAdding AccessRemoving AccessObtaining Keys and Client SecretsSOC Access Token ScriptTenantsNon-SOC Tab
Find the section relevant to the request ticket below


Creating Applications
An auth0 Application allows customer software to authenticate and interface with their Marchex stuff. These are also known as API users

NOTE: There are 3 tenants in Auth0: marchex, marchex-dev, marchex-qa and omni-dev. You can switch tenants in the top right pull-down above "create application". If the ticket doesn't specify which tenant, reply back asking for clarification and stall the ticket.
Go here
Click "Create Application"
Put the name as requested into the upper "Name" field
Select "Machine to Machine App" if nothing else is specified by the requestor
If "Machine to Machine", choose "V4 API"
Click "Create"
Fill out any specifics provided.
Send the Client ID and Client Secret via email to the person requesting the application. Don't paste them in the ticket.
You will need the Client ID again when associating the Application to an Account



Creating Enterprise Connections

SAML Connections

Go here
TBD

Other

Go here
Need to work with Shared UI/UX to figure this out, then document steps here for the specific connection



Creating Marchex Users for https://app.marchex.io
See SOC_SOP_engageSpotlightAccess


Creating Auth0 Admin Users (for managing Auth0 tenants)
Ask how long they need the access for, which tenant(s), and what application they need access to, and get CC approval for the request
Go here
For each tenant:
Click the dropdown in the upper right corner where the avatar is
Select "Switch tenant"
Select the requested tenant
Click the dropdown in the upper right corner where the avatar is
Select "Invite an Admin"
Type in the person's email, and select the application they requested access to. If it's all applications, give them access to all applications.
Click Add. The rest is up to them and they need to accept the request from their email
User will then get an email (if they don't see below "Confirmation Emails"). They will be directed to login and create a new password with the invite.
Switch the tenant back to marchex for the convenience of the next person


Confirmation Emails


As of 6/18/19, Auth0 is not sending confirmation emails when a user is added to a new Admin group. Link must be manually copied (using "Pending" link) and emailed to the user requesting access.

SOC SOP uiAuth0
SOC SOP uiNimUI | SOC SOP uiAccessPagerDuty | SOC SOP uiRT | SOC SOP uiAccessAFR | SOC SOP uiAuth0
Jump to navigationJump to search


GeneralAdding AccessRemoving AccessObtaining Keys and Client SecretsSOC Access Token ScriptTenantsNon-SOC Tab
Find the section relevant to the request ticket below


Removing Applications
Go here
Click on the application you wish to delete
Click on Settings (if you aren't already there)
Scroll to the bottom where it says <font-color=red>DANGER ZONE
Click Delete Application



Removing Users

You will need to go through all tenants and check for users AND admin users

Go here
Click on User Management and then Click on Users
Click on the user you wish to remove
Click on the "Actions" dropdown and select "Delete"
Click on "Settings" in the left-hand menu
Click the "Tenant Members" tab
Click "Remove" on the user you wish to delete
Repeat all steps for each tenant
Now we need to check the admin users for each tenant
https://manage.auth0.com/dashboard/us/qa-marchex/tenant/admins
https://manage.auth0.com/dashboard/us/omni-dev/tenant/admins
https://manage.auth0.com/dashboard/us/marchex-dev/tenant/admins
https://manage.auth0.com/dashboard/us/marchex/tenant/admins

SOC SOP uiAuth0
SOC SOP uiNimUI | SOC SOP uiAccessPagerDuty | SOC SOP uiRT | SOC SOP uiAccessAFR | SOC SOP uiAuth0

GeneralAdding AccessRemoving AccessObtaining Keys and Client SecretsSOC Access Token ScriptTenantsNon-SOC Tab
Info on Tenants and how to create them when asked for


Tenants are basically the environments within our Auth0 instance.
To change tenants:
select the drop down in the upper right where it says "marchex SO"
Click "Switch Tenant"
Select the one you want


The three tenants we use currently are:
Marchex (this is the prod account)
Marchex-qa (qa account)
Marchex-dev (dev account)
Omni-dev (app-solutions)
We really only care about access to the prod tenant. If someone wants access to qa or dev, grant it.


On occasion, someone will ask for a specific Tenant.
If they want a personal tenant, TBD
If they want a custom agreement, TBD

SOC SOP azurePortal

Follow
1

Edit

Corey Hughes
Nov 19, 2024
Description
This SOP is for adding and removing user access to various groups within portal.azure.com 

Note: The following steps allow you to easily add multiple users to a group, but in the case that you need to add one user to multiple groups, it may be faster directly from their account. Shortcut. 

== Adding Users ==

Go to portal.azure.com 
In the search bar at the top, look for Microsoft Entra ID.
Click "Groups" in the side panel. Shortcut. 
Use the search bar to look for the group name mentioned in the ticket.
Click "Members" in the side panel.
Click the "Add Members" button.
Search for the name of the user/s you need to add and click their checkbox.
Click "Select" at the bottom of the window to finalize your selections and add the users.
== Removing Users ==

Go to portal.azure.com 
In the search bar at the top, look for Microsoft Entra ID.
Click "Groups" in the side panel. Shortcut. 
Use the search bar to look for the group name mentioned in the ticket.
Click "Members" in the side panel.
Select the users you need to remove and click the "remove" button.

Adding Access

1. Log onto [Last3] .

2. Add the user to the call-scoring-login authorization group.

If they are in a group or need to be added to a group you can do that and they will automatically be added. Just sync the dynamic groups.
You might have to add them to static users if its needed.




Removing Access

1. Log onto [Last3] .

2. Remove the user to the call-scoring-login authorization group.

If they are in a group or need to be added to a group you can do that and they will automatically be added. Just sync the dynamic groups.
You might have to add them to static users if its needed.

SOC SOP uiAccessChef DataBag
SOC SOP uiAuth0 | SOC SOP azureDevOps | SOC SOP uiCallScoring | SOC SOP uiAccessChef | SOC SOP uiAccessChef DataBag
Jump to navigationJump to search
Description
This SOP is for adding and removing access for the Chef_DataBag.



Adding AccessRemoving Access


Click this link: https://github.com/marchex-chef-emu/databag_user_access_control/tree/master/items
https://github.com/enterprises/marchex-emu/sso?return_to=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fmarchex-chef-emu%2Fdatabag_user_access_control

sign in

Near the top right click Create new file button

Scroll to top of screen and put in their username.json (mine is aderrick.json)

databag_user_access_control/items/_____ or cancel
Add the following to the text box, but change UserName to their ldap alias

{
"id": "UserName"
}
Click the green Commit new file button at the bottom

Click the green Create pull request button in the middle of the screen

Wait while the checks are done, this can take a few minutes

Click the green Merge pull request button in the middle of the screen

Click the green Confirm merge button in the middle of the screen

Click the Delete branch button. It's on the right and gray.

Removing Access

Click this link: https://github.com/marchex-chef-emu/databag_user_access_control/tree/master/items
https://github.com/enterprises/marchex-emu/sso?return_to=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fmarchex-chef-emu%2Fdatabag_user_access_control

sign in

find user as (userName.json)

click it


find garbage can on far right side of the grayish bar

click it



click commit changes (green button)



click create pull request (green button)


wait while the checks are completing. It's the gold/tan text in the middle of the screen.

This might take a few minutes.

When it completes a green button (Merge Pull Request) pop up.

Click the button.


Then a green Confirm Merge button pops up.

Click it.


Then a gray Delete branch button pops up.

Click it.


At the top left of the page, you can click the blue "databag_user_access_control" again


Then click the blue folder that says items (below/left of the green clone or download button)


Verify the user's json file is gone.
next is Engage





SOC SOP engageSpotlightAccess
SOC SOP azureDevOps | SOC SOP uiCallScoring | SOC SOP uiAccessChef | SOC SOP uiAccessChef DataBag | SOC SOP engageSpotlightAccess
Jump to navigationJump to search
Quick Note for Login Error for LDAP users

It is possible LDAP passwords to go out of sync and in that case we need to ask helpdesk to re-sync the LDAP credentials for UI.
If the user is logged in and sees a message about ad|Marchex|ldapusername not found, this usually means the user isn't added in the Marchex company in the UI, and it could happen because a change of name isn't reflected in the UI. We can use the process below to check and add the user to the list.

Quick Note to understand what this is
Go UI / One UI / Engage / Spotlight are all the same website (app.marchex.io) which uses login.marchex.io for logging in. login.marchex.io is a proxy for doing authentication with Auth0. login.marchex.io is also used for authentication for Speech 1.5 and Reporting

Creating Marchex Users for https://app.marchex.io , https://qa-oneui.marchex.com/ , and https://reporting.marchex.io

This website has had many names over the years. As of October 12, 2021 it is called Engage UI. Previous names include: One UI, Go UI, Edge UI, Sales Edge UI.

Marchex Users log into this UI with their LDAP credentials. They should use their username, not their full email address.

Contractor's and Vendor's email addresses usually have a -c or -v (e.g. username-c@marchex.com) but their LDAP username is usually just 'username'


FOR PRODUCTION: You can use the https://app.marchex.io UI to create the user in production.

FOR QA ACCESS: You can use the https://qa-oneui.marchex.com/ UI to create the user in QA.


App.marchex.io-initial-screen.jpg

Navigate to People -> Users on the left hand navigation panel.

App.marchex.io-user-list.jpg

With the search Icon search for the user to make sure they haven't already been added.

If they have not been added, click the 'CREATE NEW USER' button

Fill in the email, first, last names. If the user is a contractor or vendor fill in the ldapUsername field with the appropriate username. This field should not be required, but if it is fill it in with the username. Ignore the text below the form; it does not apply to LDAP users.

App.marchex.io-user-details.jpg

Choose Marchex as the Org Unit (this is a type-ahead search box). Choose MARCHEX_STAFF as the role.

App.marchex.io-org-role-details.jpg

After you have created the newly added user can you either send them an email or add them to the CC line of the ticket and then put this into the ticket:

To login:
1. Go to app.marchex.io
2. Put your username (the part before the @marchex.com. For example I would use "aderrick" and not "aderrick@marchex.com") in the username/alias
3. Put your Marchex LDAP password for the password
4. Enjoy your new access!

SOC SOP uiGitHub
SOC SOP uiCallScoring | SOC SOP uiAccessChef | SOC SOP uiAccessChef DataBag | SOC SOP engageSpotlightAccess | SOC SOP uiGitHub
Jump to navigationJump to search

Contents
1	Description
2	Adding Access
2.1	These are the steps on how to grant access from GitHub.
2.1.1	System or App User
3	Admin Access to a Repo
4	Granting Write Access to a Repo
5	Modifying Org Access
6	Moving a Repo
7	Archiving a Repo
8	Removing Access
8.1	These are the steps on how to remove access from GitHub.
9	Notes
Description
This SOP is for adding and removing access for the GitHub.

Here is URL to access github: https://github.marchex.com/marchex-chef/

Here is URL to access New github https://github.com/marchex-chef-emu

Here is the URL to access LAST3: https://last3.marchex.com/last3/dashboard






Adding AccessAdmin Access to a RepoGranting Write Access to a RepoModifying Org AccessMoving a RepoArchiving a RepoRemoving AccessNotes
These are the steps on how to grant access from GitHub.

Note:

Both FTEs and Vendors need appropriate manager approval (New Hire tickets are implied approval).

1. Go to Last3 and see if the user is already in the "dev" security group.

If they are a vendor (non @marchex.com email address), they likely will not be


2.

If they are already in dev, they already should have access. Any write issues they may be experiencing is not access-related
If they are not in dev, and they are a vendor, go on to step 3


3. Add the user to the Last3 Authorization Group github-users. Remember to sync after the changes are made.




System or App User
1. Make sure to coordinate first with Tools to ensure this app user addition is a known task, and also to make sure there isn't additional work needed to have the access granted

2. Add the user to github-appusers last3 auth

SOC SOP uiGitHub
SOC SOP uiCallScoring | SOC SOP uiAccessChef | SOC SOP uiAccessChef DataBag | SOC SOP engageSpotlightAccess | SOC SOP uiGitHub
Jump to navigationJump to search

Contents
1	Description
2	Adding Access
2.1	These are the steps on how to grant access from GitHub.
2.1.1	System or App User
3	Admin Access to a Repo
4	Granting Write Access to a Repo
5	Modifying Org Access
6	Moving a Repo
7	Archiving a Repo
8	Removing Access
8.1	These are the steps on how to remove access from GitHub.
9	Notes
Description
This SOP is for adding and removing access for the GitHub.

Here is URL to access github: https://github.marchex.com/marchex-chef/

Here is URL to access New github https://github.com/marchex-chef-emu

Here is the URL to access LAST3: https://last3.marchex.com/last3/dashboard






Adding AccessAdmin Access to a RepoGranting Write Access to a RepoModifying Org AccessMoving a RepoArchiving a RepoRemoving AccessNotes
These are the steps on how to remove access from GitHub.

1. Is the user a Full Time Marchex user or a vendor?

Check their email address, it should be simple.
If they have an @Marchex.com alias, go to step 2.
If they are a vendor and have a non-Marchex email go to step 3.

2. Marchex Employee (marchex.com email)

If the requester is a developer they should already be in the 'dev' security group in Last3.
If the requester is not a dev, remove the user from the Last3 authorization group: github-users


3. Vendor (not a marchex.com email)

If the vendor only needed github access but NO pulley access, remove the user to the Last3 authorization group: github-restricted
If the vendor needed github access and pulley access, remove the user to the Last3 authorization group: github-restricted, then follow directions in the [pulley] .

SOC SOP Marketing Edge User Management

Follow
0

Edit

Dean Van Vlack
Mar 10
The attached PDF is a full user setup document for the Marketing Edge Platform.

For setup of SOC members, do NOT check the role - Telmetrics Administrator. Instead check the role 'Administrator' instead. Otherwise they will not be able to set up users.

The URL for Marketing Edge is https://edge.marchex.io/#/login 

Marketing Edge Internal Corporate User Access.pdf


New work item
28 visits in last 30 days
Comments
Showing filters 1 through 1




1 (800) 840-1012 | marchex.com | connect@marchex.com
© 2025 Marchex, Inc. All Rights Reserved.
Create INTERNAL MARCHEX User
To create a user, select Settings, select Users, and then select Add User:
In the Create User window, enter the following:
2 (800) 840-1012 | marchex.com | connect@marchex.com
© 2025 Marchex, Inc. All Rights Reserved.
• Username – The name the user will use to log in (use Marchex email address). This field is required.
• Email – The email address for the user. This field is required.
• Name – The user’s given name and surname. This field is required.
• Language – The user’s preferred language. This field is populated by default and optional.
• Phone – A valid phone number for the user. This field is optional.
User Roles
For internal Marchex users, you will assign the following permissions for Marketing Edge:
• Administrator – Administrators have access throughout the current Organization
• Call Detail Level - Full Detail (populated by default).
• Domain - Telmetrics Inc domain (click confirm to add to profile).
• Create - To auto-generate authentication email for new user.
• Save & Create Another - To auto-generate authentication email for new user AND re-open Create
User
• Telmetrics Administrator – Telmetrics Administrators have full, cross-Org control (ability to switch Orgs)
• NOTE: This is now a Read-Only field and has to be enabled via DB script. After the user is
created, a request will need to be sent to Production-requests@marchex.com
• Forward to the Marketing Edge DBA (marketingedge-itops@marchex.com) to run a DB
script to enable that role for the given user(s)
• Please list user names to be updated

SOC SOP uiNexus
SOC SOP engageSpotlightAccess | SOC SOP uiGitHub | SOC SOP uiAccessAdTrack | SOC SOP uiSalesEdge | SOC SOP uiNexus
Jump to navigationJump to search


Description
This SOP is for adding and removing access for Nexus and Toolsnexus.
Toolsnexus and Nexus are repositories for code builds. Nexus (old Nexus) is nexus.marchex.com. Toolsnexus (new nexus), is toolsnexus.marchex.com
Nexus is only capable of holding .jar files, whereas Toolsnexus is able to hold .jar files, gem files, docker images, and more!



Adding AccessRemoving AccessAdmin AccessUsing Nexus UIUsing toolsnexus UIFor Non-SOC People Who Want Admin Access
These are the steps on how to grant access from Nexus.

By default, all ldap users can login to nexus. These steps apply to write/publish permissions.
There are a few things to look for/ask in the request tickets.

1. If the users are in the security group DEV, they will have access.

2. If not a member of dev, they can be added to the 'nexus-dev' last3 authorization upon manager approval. Ignore that it says "Do not alter" in last3. That's from times passed and for some reason I can't modify the description (as far as I can tell, this auth group is for old nexus)

3. Ask what they want to do. IE Publish jars, publish docker images, use old nexus or new nexus (if these details are not clear already in the access request ticket)


3a. If the user is attempting, or desires, to add docker images, they will need to be added to the nexus-docker auth group in last3, which requires the user's manager's approval.. This is only for toolsnexus as old nexus does not have the capability of holding docker images
3b. If the user is attempting, or desires, to publish to toolsnexus and they are already in dev or nexus-dev, they need to be added to nexus-publish, which requires the user's manager's approval.


4. If the user is still having issues logging in, pass the ticket to Tools outlining what you've completed and ask the Tools team to investigate why the user can't log in.

nexus-admin

nexus-docker
nexus-publish




Admin AccessUsing Nexus UIUsing toolsnexus UIFor Non-SOC People Who Want Admin Access
This section is for the SOC. This is used for when devs request Admin access. If you are a Dev looking for steps, go to the "For Non-SOC People Who Want Admin Access" tab.

1. Once a request ticket is received, request approval from the MOC

2. If approval is granted, continue.

3. Go to last3 and add the user to nexus-admin. Do the usual last3 stuff with syncing, etc. Last3 SOP if needed

4. Set a reminder on the SOC calendar to remove the user's admin access after one week (compliance reasons). Add this SOP into the reminder for convenience for whoever gets to remove access.

Granting read-only access to both Prod & QA for any databases and schemas:

Login to Snowflake UI as user SOC (Pass and U/N are in bitwarden): https://sj79957.snowflakecomputing.com
In order to execute the function in the next step, make sure the correct warehouse, database and schema are selected as per attached screenshot. (warehouse = DEPLOY, database = FORTKNOX, schema = PUBLIC) Snowflake UI
Run the following command (click the Run button when ready):
CALL CREATE_USER('username', 'email');
If the onboarding was successful, it should have returned a password. Capture this and email back to user.

CALL CREATE_USER('JDOE', 'jdoe@marchex.com');


If any problems persist:

Pass the ticket to the DBA team on-call


All snowflake user management / pemissions should be handled by the DBA team if SOC needs help.

"📘 SOC Access Management – Knowledge Transfer (KT) Document
Author: Ken Boller
Last Updated: [Insert Date]
Purpose: This document provides an overview of the SOC Access Management tooling (scripts + GUI), the file structure, where it lives, and how it’s used. Intended for continuity while the primary developer is on leave.

🔧 Project Overview
The SOC Access Management project provides a streamlined way for the Security Operations Center (SOC) team to manage access across internal tools and platforms using a combination of:

A CLI tool (access_management.py)

A GUI wrapper (soctool.py)

Modular system-specific scripts (check/grant/remove)

Credential-secured operations (pending integration via Cloud Workstation VM)

📁 Repository Location
Location:
/site/socbot/scripts/ (Cloud Workstation VM)

Primary Folders:

SocTool/ → main folder for all GUI and CLI tools

access_management.py → CLI tool (entry point)

soctool.py → GUI wrapper (calls access_management.py)

Systems/UIs/ → location for individual system integration scripts (e.g., aws.py, jira.py, etc.)

Logs/ → auto-created if not present

Utils/ → shared functions (e.g., rt_api.py)

Secrets/ → will hold local credential files for authentication (set via environment variables or local config)

🔑 Authentication & Credentials (Current Status)
Cloud Workstation VM will act as the credential store.

Each system script (AWS, Jira, Grafana, etc.) will reference locally-stored secrets on the Cloud Workstation VM. These may include:

API keys

Service credentials

LDAP bind credentials

DB user/passwords for Oracle/Snowflake/etc.

⚠️ Next Step: Still awaiting access to the Cloud Workstation to complete setup and begin full integration/testing.

🧩 Script Behavior
access_management.py (CLI Tool)
Allows interactive or argument-based control of user access

Handles checking, granting, and removing access

Can be run manually or by GUI tool

Uses subprocess to call individual system scripts located in Systems/UIs/

soctool.py (GUI Tool)
Tkinter-based GUI that wraps the CLI for easier usage

Allows for user-friendly selection of check/remove/grant actions

Passes mock flag and target usernames to CLI

Individual System Scripts (e.g., aws.py, jira.py, etc.)
Each script supports: main(user, creds) and foundAccess(result) interfaces

Can be imported or executed via subprocess

Follows standard creds dict pattern:

python

creds = {
  "operatorUN": "user123",
  "accessChoice": "check/remove/grant",
  "MOCK_MODE": True/False
}

# 📘 SOC Access Management – Knowledge Transfer (KT)
**Author:** Ken Boller  
**Last Updated:** [Insert Date]  
**Audience:** SOC Engineering, DevOps, Security  

This document provides a full overview of the SOC Access Management project — including file structure, systems integrated, scripts updated/created, and how to test or run the project in production. It also outlines what's been completed, what remains, and how to maintain/extend the toolset during the author’s leave.

---

## 🧭 Project Overview

The **SOC Access Management Toolkit** allows the Security Operations Center (SOC) to manage user access across 20+ internal systems using a unified process:

- ✅ **CLI Tool** (access_management.py)
- ✅ **GUI Wrapper** (soctool.py)
- ✅ Modular per-system scripts (located in Systems/UIs/ and Systems/DBs/)
- 🔐 Credential integration pending (via **SOC Cloud Workstation**)

---

## 📁 Repository Structure

Path:  
/site/socbot/scripts/ (Located on the **SOC Cloud Workstation**)

### Folder Breakdown:
SocTool/ ├── access_management.py # CLI entry point ├── soctool.py # GUI wrapper (calls CLI) ├── Systems/ │ └── UIs/ # Contains all system-specific scripts │ ├── aws.py │ ├── jira.py │ ├── grafana.py │ └── ... ├── Utils/ │ └── rt_api.py # Reusable RT ticket interface ├── Logs/ │ └── access_management.log # Log output ├── README.md (planned) └── Secrets/ # Local credential/config files
---

## 🧹 What Was Removed

- ❌ Legacy Python 2 compatibility
- ❌ Hardcoded mock checks in scripts (replaced with standard MOCK_MODE flag)
- ❌ Disconnected system integrations that no longer existed or applied

---

## 🔧 What Was Fixed

- ✅ Converted **all legacy scripts** from Python 2 to Python 3
- ✅ Standardized all system scripts to accept the same main(user, creds) pattern
- ✅ Added logging, subprocess handling, and mocking logic for safe testability
- ✅ Fixed deprecated subprocess usage and encoding issues

---

## 🧪 What Was Added

### ✅ Major Functional Additions
- soctool.py GUI (Tkinter)
- Unified CLI: access_management.py
- Full support for check, grant, and remove modes across all systems
- Dynamic subprocess calling of scripts via file discovery
- MOCK_MODE toggle for testing

### ✅ New System Scripts Written (from scratch or updated):

| System               | Status   |
|----------------------|----------|
| AWS IAM              | ✅ Updated |
| Grafana              | ✅ Updated |
| JIRA                 | ✅ Updated |
| NimUI (Oracle)       | ✅ Updated |
| PagerDuty            | ✅ Updated |
| RT Tickets           | ✅ Updated |
| ADTrack              | ✅ Updated |
| Auth0                | ✅ New     |
| AFR                  | ✅ New     |
| Azure Portal         | ✅ New     |
| Call Scoring         | ✅ New     |
| Chef (General)       | ✅ New     |
| Chef DataBag         | ✅ New     |
| Engage / Spotlight   | ✅ New     |
| GitHub               | ✅ New     |

# 📘 SOC Access Management – Knowledge Transfer (KT)
**Author:** Ken Boller  
**Last Updated:** March 17th 2025  
**Audience:** SOC Engineering, DevOps, Security  

This document provides a full overview of the SOC Access Management project — including file structure, systems integrated, scripts updated/created, and how to test or run the project in production. It also outlines what's been completed, what remains, and how to maintain/extend the toolset during the author’s leave.

---

## 🧭 Project Overview

The **SOC Access Management Toolkit** allows the Security Operations Center (SOC) to manage user access across 20+ internal systems using a unified process:

- ✅ **CLI Tool** (access_management.py)
- ✅ **GUI Wrapper** (soctool.py)
- ✅ Modular per-system scripts (located in Systems/UIs/ and Systems/DBs/)
- 🔐 Credential integration pending (via **SOC Cloud Workstation**)

---

## 📁 Repository Structure

Path:  
https://github.com/marchex-emu/socbot/tree/restructuring/SocTool

### Folder Breakdown:

bash
SocTool/
├── access_management.py      # CLI entry point for checking, granting, removing access
├── soctool.py                # GUI wrapper that calls the CLI interactively
├── Systems/
│   ├── UIs/                  # System integration scripts (API-based or UI tools)
│   │   ├── aws.py
│   │   ├── jira.py
│   │   ├── grafana.py
│   │   ├── adtrack.py
│   │   ├── ...

│       ├── snowflake.py
│       └── ...

│   └── access_management.log # Auto-generated log of actions and outputs
└── README.md                 # (Planned) Project overview and onboarding guide

# [System Name] Access Script

**Script:** SCRIPT_FILENAME.py  
**System Type:** [UI / DB / API / Hybrid]  
**Supports:** ✅ check / ✅ grant / ✅ remove  
**Mock Mode Compatible:** ✅  
**Script Location:** Systems/[UIs|DBs]/SCRIPT_FILENAME.py

---

## 🧠 Purpose
Briefly describe what this script is for.  
For example:
> This script is used to manage access to the [System Name] platform through API calls and user lookup endpoints.

---

## ⚙️ Supported Actions

| Action     | Description |
|------------|-------------|
| check    | Verifies if the user has access to the system |
| grant    | Grants user access via API/database/add-to-group |
| remove   | Removes user access via appropriate mechanism |

---

## 🔑 Requirements

- Must be run from the **SOC Cloud Workstation**
- Requires local credentials via secret.get_secret("KEY_NAME")
- Operator credentials required for access to this system

---

## 🧪 Sample Usage

### Embedded from another script:

python
creds = {
  "operatorUN": "kboller",
  "accessChoice": "grant",
  "MOCK_MODE": False
}
main("jdoe", creds)


CLI Example:
bash
Copy
Edit
python access_management.py grant jdoe --system grafana
📎 Notes
If MOCK_MODE is set to True, no real actions will be taken.

The script logs to Logs/access_management.log.

Use foundAccess(result) to interpret and log the access check outcome.

Ensure the system’s API key or DB login is available through the secret store.

"""
SOC Access Management Tool (CLI Only)
---------------------------------------------------
✅ CLI-based access management for SOC.
✅ Secure LDAP authentication via Azure Key Vault.
✅ Interactive access management (Check → Remove/Grant).
✅ Independent from GUI (SOC Tool calls this script).
"""

#Example CLI Usage
#python access_management.py check kboller
#python access_management.py grant kboller --rt_ticket 12345
#python access_management.py remove kboller --mock

import argparse
import logging
import os
import subprocess
import sys
from datetime import datetime
from ldap3 import Server, Connection, NTLM, ALL, core
import getpass
#from azure.identity import DefaultAzureCredential
#from azure.keyvault.secrets import SecretClient

# ✅ Ensure UTF-8 encoding to prevent errors
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# ✅ Set up base directories
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get current script location
SYSTEMS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Systems", "UIs")  # Locate Systems/UIs folder
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")  # Correct path to Logs/
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# ✅ Set up logging
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "access_management.log")
logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, level=logging.INFO, format="%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s")

# ✅ Azure Key Vault Configuration
#KEY_VAULT_NAME = "soc-access-kv"  # Change if needed
#KV_URI = f"https://{KEY_VAULT_NAME}.vault.azure.net/"
#credential = DefaultAzureCredential()
#kv_client = SecretClient(vault_url=KV_URI, credential=credential)

# ✅ Define LDAP Server
#LDAP_SERVER = "ldaps://10.90.255.145"  # Update as needed


def authenticate_ldap():
    ldap_server = "ldap://ad.marchex.com"  # Confirm with IT if this is correct
    domain = "marchex"
    username = input("Enter LDAP username: ").strip()
    password = getpass.getpass("Enter LDAP password: ")

    user_dn = f"{domain}\\{username}"

    try:
        server = Server(ldap_server, get_info=ALL)
        conn = Connection(server, user=user_dn, password=password, authentication=NTLM, auto_bind=True)
        print(f"✅ Authenticated as {username}")
        return username
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"❌ LDAP auth failed: {e}")
        exit(1)

# ✅ Attempt to import rt_api.py (for RT ticket updates)
try:
    sys.path.insert(0, os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils"))
    from rt_api import add_comment
except ModuleNotFoundError:
    def add_comment(ticket, comment):
        logging.warning(f"RT API not found. Skipping RT ticket update: {ticket}.")
        print(f"⚠️ RT API not found. Skipping RT ticket update: {ticket}.")

# ✅ Retrieve Credentials from Azure Key Vault

# ✅ Simulated LDAP Authentication for Testing
def authenticate_ldap(username, password):
    """Simulated LDAP authentication (Always returns True for testing)."""
    print(f"✅ Simulated LDAP authentication successful for {username}.")
    return True  # Always return True for testing


# ✅ Prompt for missing inputs
def prompt_if_missing(value, prompt_text):
    """Prompt user for input if a value is missing."""
    return value if value else input(prompt_text).strip()


# ✅ Check user access
def check_user_access(target_user):
    """Checks all systems where the user has access."""
    timestamp = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
    print(f"🔹 Checking access for {target_user} at {timestamp}")
    logging.info(f"Checking access for {target_user}")

    access_list = []

    if not os.path.exists(SYSTEMS_DIR):
        print("❌ Error: 'Systems/UIs' directory not found.")
        logging.error("Systems directory missing.")
        sys.exit(1)


    for script in os.listdir(SYSTEMS_DIR):
        if script.endswith(".py") and script.startswith("check_"):
            system_name = script.replace("check_", "").replace(".py", "").capitalize()
            script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, script)

            try:
                cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
                process = subprocess.Popen(cmd, stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.PIPE, text=True, encoding="utf-8", bufsize=1)
                stdout_output, stderr_output = process.communicate()

                if stdout_output.strip():
                    print(f"✅ {system_name}: {stdout_output.strip()}")
                    access_list.append(system_name)

                if stderr_output.strip():
                    print(f"⚠️ {system_name} Error: {stderr_output.strip()}")
                    logging.error(f"{system_name} Error: {stderr_output.strip()}")

            except Exception as e:
                print(f"❌ {system_name}: Error checking access - {e}")
                logging.error(f"Error checking access for {system_name}: {e}")

    return access_list

# ✅ Remove access from a system
def remove_access(target_user, system_name, mock_mode):
    """Removes access from the selected system."""
    script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, f"remove_{system_name.lower()}.py")

    if os.path.exists(script_path):
        cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
        if mock_mode:
            cmd.append("--mock")

        subprocess.run(cmd, text=True, encoding="utf-8")
        print(f"✅ Removed access to {system_name} for {target_user}")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Remove script for {system_name} not found.")

# ✅ Grant access to a system
def grant_access(target_user, system_name, mock_mode):
    """Grants access to the selected system."""
    script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, f"grant_{system_name.lower()}.py")

    if os.path.exists(script_path):
        cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
        if mock_mode:
            cmd.append("--mock")

        subprocess.run(cmd, text=True, encoding="utf-8")
        print(f"✅ Granted access to {system_name} for {target_user}")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Grant script for {system_name} not found.")

# ✅ Main interactive workflow
def interactive_access_management(mock_mode=False):
    """Runs the interactive access management process."""

    # ✅ Simulate LDAP Credentials Instead of Fetching from Key Vault
    ldap_user = "mock_user@company.com"
    ldap_pass = "mock_password"

    # ✅ Retrieve LDAP credentials securely
    #ldap_user, ldap_pass = get_ldap_credentials()

    # ✅ Authenticate LDAP before proceeding
    if not authenticate_ldap(ldap_user, ldap_pass):
        print("❌ LDAP Authentication Failed. Access Denied.")
        sys.exit(1)

    # ✅ Get the target LDAP username
    target_user = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the LDAP username of the target user: ")

    # ✅ Check access first
    access_list = check_user_access(target_user)

    if access_list:
        print("\n🔹 The user currently has access to these systems:")
        for i, system in enumerate(access_list, start=1):
            print(f"  {i}. {system}")

        # ✅ Ask if access should be removed
        remove_choice = input("\nWould you like to remove access from any of these systems? (yes/no): ").strip().lower()
        if remove_choice == "yes":
            system_to_remove = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the system name to remove access from: ")
            if system_to_remove in access_list:
                remove_access(target_user, system_to_remove)
            else:
                print("❌ Invalid selection. System not found in the access list.")

    # ✅ Ask if access should be granted
    grant_choice = input("\nWould you like to grant access to a new system? (yes/no): ").strip().lower()
    if grant_choice == "yes":
        system_to_grant = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the system name to grant access to: ")
        grant_access(target_user, system_to_grant)

    print("\n🔹 Access management completed.")

# ✅ CLI Argument Parsing
if __name__ == "__main__":
    operatorUN = authenticate_ldap()
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Manage SOC user access with LDAP authentication.")
    parser.add_argument("--mock", action="store_true", help="Enable mock mode (for testing)")

    args = parser.parse_args()

    # ✅ Pass args.mock as an argument to interactive_access_management
    interactive_access_management(mock_mode=args.mock)




import json
import os
import logging

SECRETS_FILE = os.environ.get("SOC_SECRET_FILE", "/site/socbot/scripts/SocTool/Secrets/secrets.json")

def get_secret(key):
    """Retrieve secret from local JSON file."""
    try:
        with open(os.path.expanduser("~/soc-secrets/creds.json")) as f:
            secrets = json.load(f)
        return secrets.get(key)
    except Exception as e:
        raise Exception(f"Error loading secret '{key}': {e}")
        
        with open(SECRETS_FILE, 'r') as f:
            secrets = json.load(f)
        return secrets.get(key)
    except FileNotFoundError:
        logging.error(f"Secrets file not found at {SECRETS_FILE}")
    except json.JSONDecodeError:
        logging.error("Secrets file is not valid JSON.")
    return None

"""
SOC Access Management Tool (CLI Only)
---------------------------------------------------
✅ CLI-based access management for SOC.
✅ Secure LDAP authentication via Azure Key Vault.
✅ Interactive access management (Check → Remove/Grant).
✅ Independent from GUI (SOC Tool calls this script).
"""

#Example CLI Usage
#python access_management.py check kboller
#python access_management.py grant kboller --rt_ticket 12345
#python access_management.py remove kboller --mock

import argparse
import logging
import os
import subprocess
import sys
import getpass
from datetime import datetime
from ldap3 import Server, Connection, NTLM, ALL, core
from secret import get_secret


# ✅ Ensure UTF-8 encoding to prevent errors
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# ✅ Set up base directories
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get current script location
SYSTEMS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Systems", "UIs")  # Locate Systems/UIs folder
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")  # Correct path to Logs/
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# ✅ Set up logging
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "access_management.log")
logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, level=logging.INFO, format="%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s")

# ✅ Attempt to import rt_api.py (for RT ticket updates)
try:
    sys.path.insert(0, os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils"))
    from rt_api import add_comment
except ModuleNotFoundError:
    def add_comment(ticket, comment):
        logging.warning(f"RT API not found. Skipping RT ticket update: {ticket}.")
        print(f"⚠️ RT API not found. Skipping RT ticket update: {ticket}.")


def authenticate_ldap():
    ldap_server = "ldap://ad.marchex.com"  # Confirmed default domain controller
    ldap_user = get_secret("_LDAP_USER")
    ldap_pass = get_secret("_LDAP_PASS")

    try:
        server = Server(ldap_server, get_info=ALL)
        conn = Connection(server, user=ldap_user, password=ldap_pass, authentication=NTLM, auto_bind=True)
        print(f"✅ Authenticated to LDAP as {ldap_user}")
        return True
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"❌ LDAP auth failed: {e}")
        return False


# ✅ Prompt for missing inputs
def prompt_if_missing(value, prompt_text):
    """Prompt user for input if a value is missing."""
    return value if value else input(prompt_text).strip()


# ✅ Check user access
def check_user_access(target_user):
    """Checks all systems where the user has access."""
    timestamp = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
    print(f"🔹 Checking access for {target_user} at {timestamp}")
    logging.info(f"Checking access for {target_user}")

    access_list = []

    if not os.path.exists(SYSTEMS_DIR):
        print("❌ Error: 'Systems/UIs' directory not found.")
        logging.error("Systems directory missing.")
        sys.exit(1)


    for script in os.listdir(SYSTEMS_DIR):
        if script.endswith(".py") and script.startswith("check_"):
            system_name = script.replace("check_", "").replace(".py", "").capitalize()
            script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, script)

            try:
                cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
                process = subprocess.Popen(cmd, stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.PIPE, text=True, encoding="utf-8", bufsize=1)
                stdout_output, stderr_output = process.communicate()

                if stdout_output.strip():
                    print(f"✅ {system_name}: {stdout_output.strip()}")
                    access_list.append(system_name)

                if stderr_output.strip():
                    print(f"⚠️ {system_name} Error: {stderr_output.strip()}")
                    logging.error(f"{system_name} Error: {stderr_output.strip()}")

            except Exception as e:
                print(f"❌ {system_name}: Error checking access - {e}")
                logging.error(f"Error checking access for {system_name}: {e}")

    return access_list

# ✅ Remove access from a system
def remove_access(target_user, system_name, mock_mode):
    """Removes access from the selected system."""
    script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, f"remove_{system_name.lower()}.py")

    if os.path.exists(script_path):
        cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
        if mock_mode:
            cmd.append("--mock")

        subprocess.run(cmd, text=True, encoding="utf-8")
        print(f"✅ Removed access to {system_name} for {target_user}")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Remove script for {system_name} not found.")

# ✅ Grant access to a system
def grant_access(target_user, system_name, mock_mode):
    """Grants access to the selected system."""
    script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, f"grant_{system_name.lower()}.py")

    if os.path.exists(script_path):
        cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
        if mock_mode:
            cmd.append("--mock")

        subprocess.run(cmd, text=True, encoding="utf-8")
        print(f"✅ Granted access to {system_name} for {target_user}")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Grant script for {system_name} not found.")

# ✅ Main interactive workflow
def interactive_access_management(mock_mode=False):
    """Runs the interactive access management process."""

    # ✅ Simulate LDAP Credentials Instead of Fetching from Key Vault
    ldap_user = "mock_user@company.com"
    ldap_pass = "mock_password"

    # ✅ Retrieve LDAP credentials securely
    #ldap_user, ldap_pass = get_ldap_credentials()

    # ✅ Authenticate LDAP before proceeding
    if not authenticate_ldap(ldap_user, ldap_pass):
        print("❌ LDAP Authentication Failed. Access Denied.")
        sys.exit(1)

    # ✅ Get the target LDAP username
    target_user = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the LDAP username of the target user: ")

    # ✅ Check access first
    access_list = check_user_access(target_user)

    if access_list:
        print("\n🔹 The user currently has access to these systems:")
        for i, system in enumerate(access_list, start=1):
            print(f"  {i}. {system}")

        # ✅ Ask if access should be removed
        remove_choice = input("\nWould you like to remove access from any of these systems? (yes/no): ").strip().lower()
        if remove_choice == "yes":
            system_to_remove = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the system name to remove access from: ")
            if system_to_remove in access_list:
                remove_access(target_user, system_to_remove)
            else:
                print("❌ Invalid selection. System not found in the access list.")

    # ✅ Ask if access should be granted
    grant_choice = input("\nWould you like to grant access to a new system? (yes/no): ").strip().lower()
    if grant_choice == "yes":
        system_to_grant = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the system name to grant access to: ")
        grant_access(target_user, system_to_grant)

    print("\n🔹 Access management completed.")

# ✅ CLI Argument Parsing
if __name__ == "__main__":
    if not authenticate_ldap():
        print("❌ LDAP authentication failed.")
        sys.exit(1)

    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Manage SOC user access with LDAP authentication.")
    parser.add_argument("--mock", action="store_true", help="Enable mock mode (for testing)")

    args = parser.parse_args()

    # ✅ Pass args.mock as an argument to interactive_access_management
    interactive_access_management(mock_mode=args.mock)
"""

---------------------------------------------------

"""

#Example CLI Usage
#python access_management.py check kboller

#python access_management.py remove kboller --mock

import argparse
import logging
import os
import subprocess
import sys
import getpass
from datetime import datetime
from ldap3 import Server, Connection, NTLM, ALL, core
from secret import get_secret


# ✅ Ensure UTF-8 encoding to prevent errors
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# ✅ Set up base directories
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get current script location
SYSTEMS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Systems", "UIs")  # Locate Systems/UIs folder
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")  # Correct path to Logs/
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# ✅ Set up logging
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "access_management.log")
logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, level=logging.INFO, format="%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s")

required_keys = ["_LDAP_USER", "_LDAP_PASS", "_JIRA_API_KEY", "_GRAFANA_API_KEY"]
for key in required_keys:
    if not get_secret(key):
        print(f"⚠️ Missing required secret: {key}")
        sys.exit(1)


# ✅ Attempt to import rt_api.py (for RT ticket updates)
try:
    sys.path.insert(0, os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils"))
    from rt_api import add_comment
except ModuleNotFoundError:
    def add_comment(ticket, comment):
        logging.warning(f"RT API not found. Skipping RT ticket update: {ticket}.")
        print(f"⚠️ RT API not found. Skipping RT ticket update: {ticket}.")


def authenticate_ldap():
    ldap_server = "ldap://ad.marchex.com"  # Confirmed default domain controller
    ldap_user = get_secret("_LDAP_USER")
    ldap_pass = get_secret("_LDAP_PASS")

    try:
        server = Server(ldap_server, get_info=ALL)
        conn = Connection(server, user=ldap_user, password=ldap_pass, authentication=NTLM, auto_bind=True)
        print(f"✅ Authenticated to LDAP as {ldap_user}")
        return True
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"❌ LDAP auth failed: {e}")
        return False


# ✅ Prompt for missing inputs
def prompt_if_missing(value, prompt_text):
    """Prompt user for input if a value is missing."""
    return value if value else input(prompt_text).strip()


# ✅ Check user access
def check_user_access(target_user):
    """Checks all systems where the user has access."""
    timestamp = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
    print(f"🔹 Checking access for {target_user} at {timestamp}")
    logging.info(f"Checking access for {target_user}")

    access_list = []

    if not os.path.exists(SYSTEMS_DIR):
        print("❌ Error: 'Systems/UIs' directory not found.")
        logging.error("Systems directory missing.")
        sys.exit(1)


    for script in os.listdir(SYSTEMS_DIR):
        if script.endswith(".py") and script.startswith("check_"):
            system_name = script.replace("check_", "").replace(".py", "").capitalize()
            script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, script)

            try:
                cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
                process = subprocess.Popen(cmd, stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.PIPE, text=True, encoding="utf-8", bufsize=1)
                stdout_output, stderr_output = process.communicate()

                if stdout_output.strip():
                    print(f"✅ {system_name}: {stdout_output.strip()}")
                    access_list.append(system_name)

                if stderr_output.strip():
                    print(f"⚠️ {system_name} Error: {stderr_output.strip()}")
                    logging.error(f"{system_name} Error: {stderr_output.strip()}")

            except Exception as e:
                print(f"❌ {system_name}: Error checking access - {e}")
                logging.error(f"Error checking access for {system_name}: {e}")

    return access_list

# ✅ Remove access from a system
def remove_access(target_user, system_name, mock_mode):
    """Removes access from the selected system."""
    script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, f"remove_{system_name.lower()}.py")

    if os.path.exists(script_path):
        cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
        if mock_mode:
            cmd.append("--mock")

        subprocess.run(cmd, text=True, encoding="utf-8")
        print(f"✅ Removed access to {system_name} for {target_user}")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Remove script for {system_name} not found.")

# ✅ Grant access to a system
def grant_access(target_user, system_name, mock_mode):
    """Grants access to the selected system."""
    script_path = os.path.join(SYSTEMS_DIR, f"grant_{system_name.lower()}.py")

    if os.path.exists(script_path):
        cmd = ["python", script_path, target_user]
        if mock_mode:
            cmd.append("--mock")

        subprocess.run(cmd, text=True, encoding="utf-8")
        print(f"✅ Granted access to {system_name} for {target_user}")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Grant script for {system_name} not found.")

# ✅ Main interactive workflow
def interactive_access_management(mock_mode=False):
    """Runs the interactive access management process."""

    # 🔐 Pull real LDAP credentials from creds.json
    ldap_user = get_secret("_LDAP_USER")
    ldap_pass = get_secret("_LDAP_PASS")

    # ✅ Authenticate LDAP before proceeding
    if not authenticate_ldap(ldap_user, ldap_pass):
        print("❌ LDAP Authentication Failed. Access Denied.")
        sys.exit(1)

    # ✅ Get the target LDAP username
    target_user = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the LDAP username of the target user: ")

    # ✅ Check access first
    access_list = check_user_access(target_user)

    if access_list:
        print("\n🔹 The user currently has access to these systems:")
        for i, system in enumerate(access_list, start=1):
            print(f"  {i}. {system}")

        # ✅ Ask if access should be removed
        remove_choice = input("\nWould you like to remove access from any of these systems? (yes/no): ").strip().lower()
        if remove_choice == "yes":
            system_to_remove = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the system name to remove access from: ")
            if system_to_remove in access_list:
                remove_access(target_user, system_to_remove)
            else:
                print("❌ Invalid selection. System not found in the access list.")

    # ✅ Ask if access should be granted
    grant_choice = input("\nWould you like to grant access to a new system? (yes/no): ").strip().lower()
    if grant_choice == "yes":
        system_to_grant = prompt_if_missing(None, "Enter the system name to grant access to: ")
        grant_access(target_user, system_to_grant)

    print("\n🔹 Access management completed.")

# ✅ CLI Argument Parsing
if __name__ == "__main__":
    if not authenticate_ldap():
        print("❌ LDAP authentication failed.")
        sys.exit(1)

    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Manage SOC user access with LDAP authentication.")
    parser.add_argument("--mock", action="store_true", help="Enable mock mode (for testing)")

    args = parser.parse_args()

    # ✅ Pass args.mock as an argument to interactive_access_management
    interactive_access_management(mock_mode=args.mock)
"""
SOC Access Management Tool (CLI Only)
---------------------------------------------------
✅ CLI-based access management for SOC.
✅ Secure LDAP authentication via Azure Key Vault.
✅ Interactive access management (Check → Remove/Grant).
✅ Independent from GUI (SOC Tool calls this script).
"""

#Example CLI Usage
#python access_management.py check kboller
#python access_management.py grant kboller --rt_ticket 12345
#python access_management.py remove kboller --mock

import argparse
import logging
import os
import subprocess
import sys
import getpass
from datetime import datetime
from ldap3 import Server, Connection, NTLM, ALL, core
from secret import get_secret


# ✅ Ensure UTF-8 encoding to prevent errors
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# ✅ Set up base directories
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get current script location
SYSTEMS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Systems", "UIs")  # Locate Systems/UIs folder
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")  # Correct path to Logs/
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# ✅ Set up logging
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "access_management.log")
logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, level=logging.INFO, format="%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s")

required_keys = ["_LDAP_USER", "_LDAP_PASS", "_JIRA_API_KEY", "_GRAFANA_API_KEY"]
for key in required_keys:
    if not get_secret(key):
        print(f"⚠️ Missing required secret: {key}")
        sys.exit(1)


# ✅ Attempt to import rt_api.py (for RT ticket updates)
try:
    sys.path.insert(0, os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils"))
    from rt_api import add_comment
except ModuleNotFoundError:
    def add_comment(ticket, comment):
        logging.warning(f"RT API not found. Skipping RT ticket update: {ticket}.")
        print(f"⚠️ RT API not found. Skipping RT ticket update: {ticket}.")

        conn = Connection(server, user=ldap_user, password=ldap_pass, authentication=NTLM, auto_bind=True)

    except Exception as e:

        return False

"""
SOC Access Management Tool (GUI)
----------------------------------------------------
✅ Provides a GUI wrapper for access_management.py.
✅ Enforces LDAP authentication before executing actions.
✅ Calls access_management.py for check, grant, and remove actions.
✅ Mock mode enabled by default for safety.
✅ Optional RT Ticket logging.
"""

import sys
import os
import subprocess
import threading
import logging
import tkinter as tk
from tkinter import messagebox, scrolledtext
from ldap3 import Server, Connection, SIMPLE, AUTO_BIND_NO_TLS

# ✅ Set up base directories
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  
LOGS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")
ACCESS_SCRIPT = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "access_management.py")

# ✅ Ensure Logs directory exists
os.makedirs(LOGS_DIR, exist_ok=True)

# ✅ Set up logging
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOGS_DIR, "soctool.log")
logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, level=logging.INFO, format="%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s")

LDAP_SERVER = "ldaps://10.90.255.145"  # Update as needed


# ✅ LDAP Authentication Check
def authenticate_ldap(username, password):
    """Authenticate the user via LDAP before proceeding with actions."""
    try:
        server = Server(LDAP_SERVER, get_info=None)
        conn = Connection(server, user=username, password=password, authentication=SIMPLE, auto_bind=AUTO_BIND_NO_TLS)
        return conn.bound  # True if authentication succeeds
    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ LDAP authentication failed for {username}: {e}")
        return False


# ✅ Function to execute access_management.py
def execute_access_action(action, ldap_user, ldap_pass, target_user, rt_ticket, mock_mode, log_area):
    """Runs access_management.py in a subprocess and updates GUI logs."""

    def run():
        try:
            # ✅ Validate LDAP credentials first
            if not authenticate_ldap(ldap_user, ldap_pass):
                log_area.insert(tk.END, "❌ Invalid LDAP credentials! Aborting.\n", "error")
                log_area.see(tk.END)
                return

            args = [ldap_user, ldap_pass, target_user]
            if rt_ticket:
                args.extend(["--rt_ticket", rt_ticket])
            if mock_mode:
                args.append("--mock")

            process = subprocess.Popen(
                ["python", ACCESS_SCRIPT, action] + args,
                stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
                stderr=subprocess.PIPE,
                text=True,
                encoding="utf-8",
                bufsize=1
            )

            for line in iter(process.stdout.readline, ""):
                log_area.insert(tk.END, line.strip() + "\n")
                log_area.see(tk.END)

            for line in iter(process.stderr.readline, ""):
                log_area.insert(tk.END, f"⚠️ {line.strip()}\n")
                log_area.see(tk.END)

            process.stdout.close()
            process.stderr.close()
            process.wait()

        except Exception as e:
            log_area.insert(tk.END, f"❌ Error: {str(e)}\n", "error")
            logging.error(f"Error executing {ACCESS_SCRIPT}: {str(e)}")

    thread = threading.Thread(target=run, daemon=True)
    thread.start()


# ✅ Function to create GUI window for actions
def open_access_window(action, show_mock_mode=True):
    """Creates a GUI window to handle access actions."""

    action_window = tk.Toplevel(root)
    action_window.title(f"SOC - {action.capitalize()} Access")
    action_window.geometry("500x525")

    tk.Label(action_window, text=f"{action.capitalize()} User Access", font=("Arial", 14, "bold")).pack(pady=10)

    # ✅ LDAP Credentials
    tk.Label(action_window, text="Your LDAP Username:").pack()
    ldap_user_entry = tk.Entry(action_window, width=40)
    ldap_user_entry.pack(pady=5)

    tk.Label(action_window, text="Your LDAP Password:").pack()
    ldap_pass_entry = tk.Entry(action_window, width=40, show="*")
    ldap_pass_entry.pack(pady=5)

    # ✅ Target User
    tk.Label(action_window, text="Target LDAP Username:").pack()
    target_user_entry = tk.Entry(action_window, width=40)
    target_user_entry.pack(pady=5)

    # ✅ RT Ticket (Optional)
    tk.Label(action_window, text="Enter RT Ticket Number (Optional):").pack()
    rt_ticket_entry = tk.Entry(action_window, width=40)
    rt_ticket_entry.pack(pady=5)

    # ✅ Mock Mode (Enabled by default)
    mock_mode = tk.BooleanVar(value=True)
    if show_mock_mode:
        tk.Checkbutton(action_window, text="Enable Mock Mode", variable=mock_mode).pack()

    # ✅ Log Display
    tk.Label(action_window, text="Logs:").pack()
    log_area = tk.Text(action_window, width=60, height=10)
    log_area.pack(pady=5)

    def execute_action():
        """Executes the access action when the button is clicked."""
        ldap_user = ldap_user_entry.get().strip()
        ldap_pass = ldap_pass_entry.get().strip()
        target_user = target_user_entry.get().strip()
        rt_ticket = rt_ticket_entry.get().strip() if rt_ticket_entry.get().strip() else None

        if not ldap_user or not ldap_pass or not target_user:
            messagebox.showerror("Error", "LDAP username, password, and target user are required.")
            return

        log_area.insert(tk.END, f"🚀 Running {action} access script for {target_user}...\n")
        log_area.see(tk.END)

        execute_access_action(action, ldap_user, ldap_pass, target_user, rt_ticket, mock_mode.get(), log_area)

    tk.Button(action_window, text="Execute", command=execute_action, font=("Arial", 12), width=20).pack(pady=10)


# ✅ Function to open RT queue clearing window
def open_clear_rt_window():
    """Opens a GUI window to display RT queue clearing process in real-time."""

    rt_window = tk.Toplevel(root)
    rt_window.title("Clearing RT Queue")
    rt_window.geometry("600x400")

    tk.Label(rt_window, text="Processing RT Queue...", font=("Arial", 14, "bold")).pack(pady=10)

    log_area = scrolledtext.ScrolledText(rt_window, width=70, height=15)
    log_area.pack(pady=5)

    execute_script("clear_rt", [], log_area)


# ✅ GUI Window Setup
root = tk.Tk()
root.title("SOC Access Management")
root.geometry("400x350")
root.resizable(False, False)

tk.Label(root, text="SOC Access Management", font=("Arial", 14, "bold")).pack(pady=20)

tk.Button(root, text="Check User Access", font=("Arial", 12),
          command=lambda: open_access_window("check", show_mock_mode=False), width=25, height=2).pack(pady=5)

tk.Button(root, text="Grant User Access", font=("Arial", 12),
          command=lambda: open_access_window("grant", show_mock_mode=True), width=25, height=2).pack(pady=5)

tk.Button(root, text="Remove User Access", font=("Arial", 12),
          command=lambda: open_access_window("remove", show_mock_mode=True), width=25, height=2).pack(pady=5)

tk.Button(root, text="Clear RT Queue", font=("Arial", 12),
          command=lambda: open_clear_rt_window(), width=25, height=2).pack(pady=5)

# ✅ Start GUI
root.mainloop()
